style=\"top:;bottom:;left:;right:;width:922px;height:auto;position:;pointer-events:none\" class=\"txtNew\" id=\"comp-k5r3fs9t\"><h4 class=\"font_4\" style=\"font-size:22px; line-height:1.4em;\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Carbon statement</span></h4>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\">The Knights Lab offsets all carbon emissions for all work-related flights.&nbsp;</p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\">Offsetting your flight's carbon footprint is easy:</p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></p>\n\n<ol class=\"font_8\">\n\t<li>\n\t<p class=\"font_8\">Calculate the emissions of your flight per passenger using the <span style=\"text-decoration:underline;\"><a href=\"https://www.icao.int/environmental-protection/Carbonoffset/Pages/default.aspx\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://www.icao.int/environmental-protection/Carbonoffset/Pages/default.aspx\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\">ICAO calculator</a></span>,&nbsp;or use this rule of thumb: a typical round-trip domestic flight emits around 1,000 lbs or less of carbon per passenger; a typical international flight emits around 2,000 lbs or less of carbon per passenger.&nbsp;</p>\n\t</li>\n\t<li>\n\t<p class=\"font_8\">Purchase audited carbon offsets at <span style=\"text-decoration:underline;\"><a href=\"https://www.terrapass.com/product/productindividuals-families\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://www.terrapass.com/product/productindividuals-families\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\">terrapass.com</a></span>. Currently this will cost $5 per 1,000 pounds, so $5 for a domestic flight and $10 for an international flight. Make your flight carbon-negative by doubling the amount.</p>\n\t</li>\n\t<li>\n\t<p class=\"font_8\">Don't forget to&nbsp;spread the word after you make your purchase!</p>\n\t</li>\n</ol>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></p></div><div data-packed=\"true\" style=\"top:;bottom:;left:;right:;width:399px;height:auto;position:;pointer-events:none\" class=\"txtNew\" id=\"WRchTxt1n-1dsv\"><h4 style=\"font-size:14px; font-weight:normal;\">\u00b7</span><span style=\"font-size:14px; font-weight:normal;\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">ing <span style=\"font-size:12px;\">[HAK-</span></span><span style=\"font-size:12px;\">ing<span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">]</span></span></span></h4>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\">&nbsp;</p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\"><span class=\"color_21\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">1.</span></span>Writing&nbsp;or refining computer programs skillfully.</p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\">&nbsp;</p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\"><span class=\"color_21\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">2.</span></span>Seeking and exploiting weaknesses in a complex system in order to change its behavior for one's benefit.</p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\">&nbsp;</p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\"><span style=\"text-decoration:underline;\">Our computational microbiology lab develops methods that&nbsp;<span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">bring&nbsp;precision medicine to the microbiome.</span></span>&nbsp;We apply&nbsp;those methods to find&nbsp;patterns in microbial communities that predict and diagnose human diseases.</p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\">&nbsp;</p></div><div id=\"StBttna-t1g\" data-align=\"center\" data-disabled=\"false\" data-margin=\"0\" data-should-use-flex=\"true\" data-width=\"160\" >The first paper from the Immigrant Microbiome Project was recently&nbsp;<span style=\\\"text-decoration:underline;\\\"><a dataquery=\\\"#txtMedia1erc\\\">published in the journal Cell<\\/a><\\/span>. science more inclusive for Hmong and Karen populations in the US by investigating the link between the microbiome, and diabetes and obesity in immigrant populations, as well as first and second generations, who have much higher rates of diabetes and obesity when compared to the general population of the US. >The first paper from the Immigrant Microbiome Project was recently&nbsp;<span style=\\\"text-decoration:underline;\\\"><a dataquery=\\\"#txtMedia1erc\\\">published in the journal Cell<\\/a><\\/span>. science more inclusive for Hmong and Karen populations in the US by investigating the link between the microbiome, and diabetes and obesity in immigrant populations, as well as first and second generations, who have much higher rates of diabetes and obesity when compared to the general population of the US. Her study, the Immigrant Microbiome Project, adds diversity, cultural awareness, and community to a field of science that is not often accessible to immigrant communities. During her time at the University of Minnesota, PJ has embraced every hurdle to becoming a scientist in the computational biology field, and soon she will be defending her thesis, then will be heading off to a new endeavor into science-based public policy as Miss Pajau Vangay, Ph.D. And we wish her nothing but the
